<div id="review_166528078" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/166528078" />
    <a title="Emily Blake" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2888791-emily-blake"><img alt="Emily Blake" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1256783944p2/2888791.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/166528078?book_show_action=true">May 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emily Blake" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emily Blake" href="/user/show/2888791-emily-blake">Emily Blake</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback " href="/book/show/612417.The_Irresistible_Revolution">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2888791-emily-blake?shelf=religious">religious</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer166528078" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17525655128208282269">The Irresistible Revolution started off fairly well. Shane has done a lot of cool things with his life and no one can deny that he's doing a wonderful job of living radically. He seems to be one of those people who really lives out his beliefs and that's hard to find these days. A lot of the stuff in this book really made me think. Let me give you some quotes that I found really challenging:<br/><br/><br/>"Jesus never says to the poor, come find the church, but he says to those of us in the church, go into the</span>
  <span id="freeText17525655128208282269" style="display:none">The Irresistible Revolution started off fairly well. Shane has done a lot of cool things with his life and no one can deny that he's doing a wonderful job of living radically. He seems to be one of those people who really lives out his beliefs and that's hard to find these days. A lot of the stuff in this book really made me think. Let me give you some quotes that I found really challenging:<br /><br /><br />"Jesus never says to the poor, come find the church, but he says to those of us in the church, go into the world and find the poor, hungry, homeless, imprisoned, Jesus in his disguises." p 102<br /><br />"The tragedy in the church is not that rich Christians do not care about the poor but that the rich Christians do not know the poor."<br /><br />"Even if there were no heaven and there were no hell, would you still follow Jesus? would you follow him for the joy and fulfillment he gives you right now?"<br /><br />I think you can get a pretty good idea of the drift of the book by reading these quotes. It's always good to hear/read stuff like this to give yourself a little bit of a shake. These are things that people should think about, and they're much to easy to push to the back of your mind.<br /><br />To be honest tho I didn't finish the book. As it progressed it began to get more and more about all the things Shane Claiborne knew, and all the sins he was able to point out to people. He started to talk about washing machines ran by bicycles and about how people who try to make money are misguided. Maybe I'm taking these things out of context, but that was the definite vibe I was getting so couldn't make myself go on. <br /><br />I think if you're looking for a book about living radically for God, then maybe Radical by David Platt is one I'd pick over this one.<br /><br />Props to Shane tho! I think what he's doing/has done is great. And his house church ministry sounds really neat.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17525655128208282269" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_23063163" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer23063163" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10847782090207772536">An impressionistic review of an impressionistic book:<br/><br/>I finished <i>Irresistible Revolution</i> shortly after debating Gitmo with a friend from church. He argued that we should trust our executive branch to do the right thing, and that innocent casualties in a war are worth the expense. They aren't US citizens, after all.<br/><br/>This book would not change that friend's mind about anything. Indeed, I disagree with a lot of what Claiborne says. But I found the book oddly soothing after that debate. Strange as it </span>
  <span id="freeText10847782090207772536" style="display:none">An impressionistic review of an impressionistic book:<br /><br />I finished <i>Irresistible Revolution</i> shortly after debating Gitmo with a friend from church. He argued that we should trust our executive branch to do the right thing, and that innocent casualties in a war are worth the expense. They aren't US citizens, after all.<br /><br />This book would not change that friend's mind about anything. Indeed, I disagree with a lot of what Claiborne says. But I found the book oddly soothing after that debate. Strange as it is to say, it is good to be reminded that some people who love Jesus are still willing to try to love their enemies even at great cost. So it helped me calm down after a rather disappointing conversation.<br /><br />Lest anyone misunderstand, warfare is only a small part of the book. Most of the book is devoted to Claiborne's call for economic reform and community life. I could quibble about specifics endlessly. But that would be mostly missing the point.</span>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review23063163">

<div id="review_1632101" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1632101" />
    <a title="Tom" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78287-tom"><img alt="Tom" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502554440p2/78287.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1632101?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tom" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tom" href="/user/show/78287-tom">Tom</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78287-tom?shelf=non-fiction">non-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78287-tom?shelf=christianity">christianity</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1632101" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16727087964484092453">Very inspiring, a book about getting back to the root of what it means to be a Christian, i.e. living with "the least of these" and fighting for peace and justice. However, the book is marred by its youth-pastor-esque voice of excitement and by Zondervan's over-marketing (just look at the fake duct tape on the cover).<br/><br/>Also, as a former resident in an intentional Christian community in a poor neighborhood, his stories of his own life are rosy and idealistic. Claiborne never mentions the difficulty</span>
  <span id="freeText16727087964484092453" style="display:none">Very inspiring, a book about getting back to the root of what it means to be a Christian, i.e. living with "the least of these" and fighting for peace and justice. However, the book is marred by its youth-pastor-esque voice of excitement and by Zondervan's over-marketing (just look at the fake duct tape on the cover).<br /><br />Also, as a former resident in an intentional Christian community in a poor neighborhood, his stories of his own life are rosy and idealistic. Claiborne never mentions the difficulty in overcoming racial boundaries (they seem to just disappear when one tries) or getting involved in neighbors' family disputes.<br /><br />Still, I recommend this book to anyone interested in an authentic picture of Christianity outside of the fundamentalist caricatures found in pulpits nationwide, and even the Oval Office.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16727087964484092453" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1913099467" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1913099467" />
    <a title="Steven Jacke" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13342036-steven-jacke"><img alt="Steven Jacke" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470500818p2/13342036.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1913099467?book_show_action=true">Apr 09, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steven Jacke" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steven Jacke" href="/user/show/13342036-steven-jacke">Steven Jacke</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/28263385-the-irresistible-revolution-updated-and-expanded">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13342036-steven-jacke?shelf=read-christian">read-christian</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1913099467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16742366701957631115">In a post-evangelical-support-for-Trump America, I've had some crisis of faith, and I've been rereading a lot of books from my youthful energetic days, and this was one of them. It took me awhile to read because I kept escaping into fun sci-fi books rather than stay in the real world. <br/><br/>What can I say? I'm a Shane Claiborne fan. I'm just old and tired, and not really in the mood to go to Iraq to protest war. I just want to be a comfortable Christian, vote the right way, and enjoy my Sunday afterno</span>
  <span id="freeText16742366701957631115" style="display:none">In a post-evangelical-support-for-Trump America, I've had some crisis of faith, and I've been rereading a lot of books from my youthful energetic days, and this was one of them. It took me awhile to read because I kept escaping into fun sci-fi books rather than stay in the real world. <br /><br />What can I say? I'm a Shane Claiborne fan. I'm just old and tired, and not really in the mood to go to Iraq to protest war. I just want to be a comfortable Christian, vote the right way, and enjoy my Sunday afternoons. <br /><br />This version has been updated significantly, and if you are debating reading the original or this one, go with this one. </span>

<div id="review_39995242" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39995242" />
    <a title="Nathan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1064644-nathan"><img alt="Nathan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1232389013p2/1064644.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39995242?book_show_action=true">Dec 12, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nathan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nathan" href="/user/show/1064644-nathan">Nathan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1064644-nathan?shelf=nashville-library">nashville-library</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39995242" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15937295468232341310">I don't agree with Claiborne's "generous orthodoxy" stance, but it's impossible to argue with his simple commitment to living out the Gospel in everyday life. When I finished this book, I wanted to sell all my stuff and hang out with poor people...and that's the point. If Tolstoy and Francis of Assisi hold any appeal, this book will too, as it's basically their ideas, framed for modern, post-church Christians. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('h9iqGLQektSCy34cOcTQ19s5pdpCeJLiDYRlmQx1jXwOrybaMRk595r4ZJ4GoWsu0/+co2eHXR4DeLQuE5LcQw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oJy6U8ULgrdP3o6dGYQQhGx+CmL016UHRLQ4XVzpwqop6zaRQAwplFftlB8m4at9ZLgzG9EoavtKSOnqQw6TlQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

Along the way, Foster shows that it is only by and through these practices that the true path to spiritual growth can be found.\n\nDividing the Disciplines into three movements of the Spirit, Foster shows how each of these areas contribute to a balanced spiritual life. The inward Disciplines of meditation, prayer, fasting, and study offer avenues of personal examination and change. The outward Disciplines of simplicity, solitude, submission, and service help prepare us to make the world a better place. The corporate Disciplines of confession, worship, guidance, and celebration bring us nearer to one another and to God.\n\nFoster provides a wealth of examples demonstrating how these Disciplines can become part of our daily activities—and how they can help us shed our superficial habits and &quot;bring the abundance of God into our lives.&quot; He offers crucial new insights on simplicity, demonstrating how the biblical view of simplicity, properly understood and applied, brings joy and balance to our inward and outward lives and &quot;sets us free to enjoy the provision of God as a gift that can be shared with others.&quot; The discussion of celebration, often the most neglected of the Disciplines, shows its critical importance, for it stands at the heart of the way to Christ.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/36103.Shane_Claiborne">About Shane Claiborne</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/36103.Shane_Claiborne"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1201095845p3/36103.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/36103.Shane_Claiborne">Shane Claiborne
</a></div>

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer2918065031209469388">Shane Claiborne is a prominent speaker, activist, and best-selling author. Shane worked with Mother Teresa in Calcutta, and founded The Simple Way in Philadelphia. He heads up Red Letter Christians, a movement of folks who are committed to living "as if Jesus meant the things he said." Shane is a champion for grace which has led him to jail advocating for the homeless, and to places like Iraq and </span>
  <span id="freeText2918065031209469388" style="display:none">Shane Claiborne is a prominent speaker, activist, and best-selling author. Shane worked with Mother Teresa in Calcutta, and founded The Simple Way in Philadelphia. He heads up Red Letter Christians, a movement of folks who are committed to living "as if Jesus meant the things he said." Shane is a champion for grace which has led him to jail advocating for the homeless, and to places like Iraq and Afghanistan to stand against war. And now grace fuels his passion to end the death penalty.<br /><br />Shane’s books include Jesus for President, Red Letter Revolution, Common Prayer, Follow Me to Freedom, Jesus, Bombs and Ice Cream, Becoming the Answer to Our Prayers, his classic The Irresistible Revolution and his newest book, Executing Grace. He has been featured in a number of films including "Another World Is Possible" and "Ordinary Radicals." His books have been translated into more than a dozen languages. Shane speaks over one hundred times a year, nationally and internationally. His work has appeared in Esquire, SPIN, Christianity Today, and The Wall Street Journal, and he has been on everything from Fox News and Al Jazeera to CNN and NPR. He’s given academic lectures at Harvard, Princeton, Liberty, Duke, and Notre Dame. <br /><br />Shane speaks regularly at denominational gatherings, festivals, and conferences around the globe.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2918065031209469388" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
